## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship for a material. The stress likely depends on strain through hardening behavior and on temperature through thermal softening or thermally-activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (T-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity with constant modulus)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus decrease with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (JC model without strain rate)
- Johnson-Cook thermal form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (exponential thermal softening with power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 * T)) (thermally-activated deformation)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * (c3 + c4 * T) (saturation hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear with saturation)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * log(c1 * epsilon + (c2 * epsilon**2 + 1)**0.5) (sinh-based constitutive model inverted)
- Exponential softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 * T)) * (1 + c4 * epsilon) (combined mechanisms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening behavior → Power-law form epsilon**c with 0<c<1 (work hardening exponent typically 0.1-0.5 for metals)
- Thermal softening as multiplicative factor → Stress factorizes as f(epsilon)*g(T), where g(T) is a decreasing function of T
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(-c/T) or exp(c*T) terms indicate thermally-activated dislocation mechanisms
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress represents initial yield strength independent of strain
- Saturation hardening → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicates stress approaching a saturation value at large strains
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as (1 - c*T) or (c0 - T) representing distance from melting point
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Piecewise or smooth transition near small epsilon values, linear at small strain becoming nonlinear
- Modulus-strain coupling → At finite strains, effective modulus itself may depend on strain level through damage or geometric effects

Setting c0=0, c1=0, c4=-1 gives: `T*c3*exp(-epsilon) + T*epsilon + c5*exp(c6*epsilon)`. This has `T*epsilon` which can't be eliminated and doesn't have `epsilon**3`. No match.

**Candidate 4:** `T*c0 + T*c1/(c2 + epsilon) + T*c3*exp(c4*epsilon) + T*epsilon + c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + c7*exp(c8*epsilon**c9)`

Setting c0=0, c1=0, c4=-1, c6=-1: `T*c3*exp(-epsilon) + T*epsilon + c5*exp(-epsilon) + c7*exp(c8*epsilon**c9)`. Still has `T*epsilon` that can't be removed. No.

**Candidate 43:** `T*c0 + T*c1/(c2 + epsilon) + T*c3*exp(c4*epsilon) + T*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6 + c7*epsilon**c8)`

The last term is `c5*exp(T*c6)*exp(c7*epsilon**c8)`. Setting c6=0: `c5*exp(c7*epsilon**c8)`. Setting c8=3, this gives `c5*exp(c7*epsilon**3)` which isn't `epsilon**3`. No.

**Candidate 45:** `T*c0 + T*c1/(c2 + epsilon) + T*c3*epsilon + T*c4*epsilon**2 + T*c5*epsilon**2*exp(c6*epsilon) + T**c7*c8*epsilon**c9`

Setting c0=0, c1=0, c3=0, c4=0, c5=0: leaves `T**c7*c8*epsilon**c9`. Setting c7=0: `c8*epsilon**c9` — just one term, not enough.

Need terms: `epsilon**3`, `T*exp(-epsilon)`, `exp(-epsilon)`.

**Candidate 11:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + T*c2*exp(c3*epsilon) + T*c4*log(c5*epsilon + 1) + T + c6*epsilon + c7*exp(T*c8 + c9*epsilon)`

Last term: `c7*exp(T*c8)*exp(c9*epsilon)`. Setting c8=0: `c7*exp(c9*epsilon)`. Setting c9=-1: `c7*exp(-epsilon)`.
Remaining: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + T*c2*exp(c3*epsilon) + T*c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + T + c6*epsilon + c7*exp(-epsilon)`

Setting c3=-1: `T*c2*exp(-epsilon)` ✓. Setting c0=0, c1=0, c4=0: `T*c2*exp(-epsilon) + T + c6*epsilon + c7*exp(-epsilon)`.

This gives `T + c6*epsilon + T*c2*exp(-epsilon) + c7*exp(-epsilon)`. We need `epsilon**3` but have `T` and `epsilon`. No match.

What if we keep c4? `T*c4*log(c5*epsilon+1)` — this is logarithmic, can't produce `epsilon**3`.

None of these candidates can produce `epsilon**3` as a standalone (non-T-multiplied) term alongside `T*exp(-epsilon)` and `exp(-epsilon)`.

Candidates with `T**c7*c8*epsilon**c9` (candidate 45): Setting c7=0 gives `c8*epsilon**c9 = c8*epsilon**3`. But then T terms need to produce `T*exp(-epsilon)`, and we have polynomial T terms only. No `exp` in the T-multiplied terms of what's left after zeroing.

Wait, candidate 45: `T*c5*epsilon**2*exp(c6*epsilon)` — set c6=-1 to approximate? No, need exact match, and `epsilon**2*exp(-epsilon) ≠ exp(-epsilon)`.

After thorough analysis, no candidate can produce the exact structural form `epsilon**3 + T*exp(-epsilon) + exp(-epsilon)`.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 7.317 * epsilon^3 + 7.950 * (T - 287.09) * exp(-epsilon)**

Expanding: **7.317 * epsilon^3 + 7.950 * T * exp(-epsilon) - 2283.0 * exp(-epsilon)**

So the GT has three basis functions in terms of (T, epsilon):
1. **epsilon^3** (no T dependence)
2. **T * exp(-epsilon)**
3. **exp(-epsilon)** (no T dependence)

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. I need to check if each candidate's functional form can produce exactly these three terms.

Key observations:
- Terms with T must collectively produce: T * exp(-epsilon) + 0 (no other T-dependent terms)
- Terms without T must produce: 7.317 * epsilon^3 - 2283 * exp(-epsilon)
- epsilon^3 is a critical basis function that must appear somehow

Let me check candidates that have exp(c*epsilon) terms (which can give exp(-epsilon)) and might produce epsilon^3.

**The fundamental challenge**: epsilon^3 must appear. Most candidates have polynomials in epsilon multiplied by T, rational functions in epsilon multiplied by T, or exp/log/sin terms. For epsilon^3 to appear WITHOUT T, we need terms not multiplied by T.

Let me scan for candidates that have terms independent of T that could produce epsilon^3:

Most candidates have constant terms (c), exp terms, sin terms, log terms, or rational terms independent of T - none of these can produce epsilon^3.

Candidates with terms like `c*epsilon` (independent of T) can only give linear epsilon terms, not epsilon^3.

Candidates with `c7*epsilon**c8` or `c*(epsilon)**c` terms independent of T could potentially give epsilon^3.

Let me check specific candidates:

**Candidate 43**: `T*c0 + T*c1/(c2+epsilon) + T*c3*exp(c4*epsilon) + T*epsilon + c5*exp(T*c6 + c7*epsilon**c8)`
The non-T term: c5*exp(T*c6 + c7*epsilon^c8). This has T inside exp, so it can't separate into epsilon^3 unless c6=0, giving c5*exp(c7*epsilon^c8), which is still exp, not polynomial.

The T-dependent part: T*c0 + T*c1/(c2+epsilon) + T*c3*epsilon + T*c4*epsilon^2 + T*c5*epsilon^2*exp(c6*epsilon). Setting c0, c3, c4, c5 = 0 and keeping T*c1/(c2+epsilon): this can't produce T*exp(-epsilon). **No match.**

**Candidate 9**: `T*c0 + T*c1/(c2+epsilon) + T*c3*exp(c4*epsilon) + T*epsilon + c5*exp(c6*epsilon^c7)`
Non-T terms: c5*exp(c6*epsilon^c7). This is exp, not polynomial. Cannot produce epsilon^3. **No match.**

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain a non-T-dependent term that can produce epsilon^3. The candidates have terms like constants, exp, sin, log, rational functions, or linear epsilon terms independent of T - none can generate epsilon^3. Going through all 50 candidates systematically confirms this: every polynomial power of epsilon (like epsilon^2) appears multiplied by T, and standalone (non-T) terms are limited to constants, exp, sin, log, rational, or linear epsilon terms.
